2:23:1290:0:14:72:302:700:12:Times:12:Times:A Macroeconomic Model with Financial Panics
2:24:1333:14:14:72:348:686:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:Mark Gertler, Nobuhiro Kiyotaki, and Andrea Prestipino 
2:25:1387:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 24126
2:26:1415:14:14:72:148:658:12:Times:12:g_d0_f4:December 2017

2:28:1442:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:29:1450:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:This  paper  incorporates  banks  and  banking  panics  within  a  conventional  macroeconomic 
2:30:1545:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:framework to analyze the dynamics of a financial crisis of the kind recently experienced. We are 
2:31:1641:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:particularly  interested in  characterizing  the  sudden  and  discrete  nature  of  the  banking  panics  as 
2:32:1750:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:well as the circumstances that makes an economy vulnerable to such panics in some instances but 
2:33:1845:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:not  in  others.  Having  a  conventional macroeconomic  model  allows  us  to  study  the  channels  by 
2:34:1949:14:42:72:467:518:12:Times:12:Times:which the crisis affects real activity and the effects of policies in containing crises.
2:35:2036:42:14:72:135:476:12:Times:12:Times:Mark Gertler

3:53:2373:0:37:110:235:654:17:g_d0_f5:17:g_d0_f5:1  Introduction
3:54:2388:37:15:110:494:617:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:As both Bernanke (2010) and Gorton (2010) argue, at the heartof the recent
3:55:2462:15:14:110:494:602:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nancial crisis was a series of bank runs that culminated in the precipitous
3:56:2538:14:15:110:494:588:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:demise of a number of major nancial institutions. During the period where
3:57:2612:15:14:110:494:573:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the panics were most intense in October 2008, all the major investment banks
3:58:2688:14:14:110:495:559:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:e¤ectively failed, the commercial paper market froze, and the Reserve Pri-
3:59:2762:14:15:110:494:545:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:mary Fund (a major money market fund) experienced a run. The distress
3:60:2831:15:14:110:495:530:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:quickly spilled over to the real sector.  Credit spreads roseto Great De-
3:61:2904:14:15:110:493:516:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:pression era levels. There was an immediate sharp contraction in economic
3:62:2977:15:14:110:494:501:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:activity: From 2008:Q4 through 2009:Q1 real output droppedat an eight
3:63:3046:14:15:110:495:487:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:percent annual rate, driven mainly by a nearly forty percentdrop in invest-
3:64:3121:15:14:110:493:472:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ment expenditure. Also relevant is that this sudden discrete contraction in
3:65:3196:14:15:110:495:458:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nancial and real economic activity occurred in the absenceof any apparent
3:66:3270:15:14:110:335:443:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:large exogenous disturbance to the economy.
3:67:3313:14:14:128:495:429:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:In this paper we incorporate banks and banking panics withina con-
3:68:3379:14:15:110:496:415:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ventional macroeconomic framework - a New Keynesian model with capital
3:69:3449:15:14:110:493:400:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:accumulation. Our goal is to develop a model where it is possible to analyze
3:70:3525:14:15:110:493:386:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:both qualitatively and quantitatively the dynamics of a nancial crisis of the
3:71:3603:15:14:110:493:371:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:kind recently experienced. We are particularly interestedin characterizing
3:72:3677:14:15:110:495:357:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the sudden and discrete nature of banking panics as well as the circumstances
3:73:3754:15:14:110:494:342:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:that make the economy vulnerable to such panics in some instances but not
3:74:3827:14:15:110:493:328:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:in others. Having a conventional macroeconomic model allows us to study
3:75:3898:15:14:110:494:313:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the channels by which the crisis a¤ects aggregate economic activity and the
3:76:3973:14:14:110:338:299:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:e¤ects of various policies in containing crises.
3:77:4021:14:15:128:495:285:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Our paper ts into a lengthy literature aimed at adapting core macroeco-
3:78:4093:15:14:110:495:270:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nomic models to account for nancial crises1. Much of this literature empha-
3:79:4169:14:15:110:493:256:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:sizes the role of balance sheets in constraining borrowers from spending when
3:80:4246:15:14:110:492:241:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nancial markets are imperfect. Because balance sheets tend to strengthen in
3:81:4322:14:15:110:495:227:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:booms and weaken in recessions, nancial conditions work toamplify uctu-
3:82:4395:15:14:110:494:212:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ations in real activity. Many authors have stressed that this kind of balance
3:83:4472:14:15:110:494:198:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:sheet mechanism played a central role in the crisis, particularly for banks
3:84:4547:15:14:110:496:183:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:and households, but at the height of the crisis also for non-nancial rms.
3:85:4622:14:14:110:495:169:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Nonetheless, as Mendoza (2010), He and Krishnamurthy (2017) and Brun-
3:86:4691:14:15:110:494:155:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nermeier and Sannikov (2014) have emphasized, these modelsdo not capture
3:87:4763:15:17:110:495:140:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the highly nonlinear aspect of the crisis. Although the nancial mechanisms
3:88:4838:17:0:124:489:123:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:1See Gertler and Kiyotaki (2011) and Brunnermeier et. al (2013) for recent surveys.
4:89:4922:0:15:110:492:654:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:in these papers tend to amplify the e¤ects of disturbances, they do not easily
4:90:5000:15:14:110:494:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:capture sudden discrete collapses. Nor do they tend to capture the run-like
4:91:5075:14:15:110:319:625:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:behavior associated with nancial panics.
4:92:5116:15:14:128:494:610:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Conversely, beginning with Diamond and Dybvig (1983), there is a large
4:93:5186:14:14:110:494:596:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:literature on banking panics. An important common theme of this literature
4:94:5260:14:15:110:493:582:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:is how liquidity mismatch, i.e.  partially illiquid long-term assets funded
4:95:5335:15:14:110:494:567:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:by short-term debt, opens up the possibility of runs. Most ofthe models
4:96:5406:14:15:110:495:553:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:in this literature, though, are partial equilibrium and highly stylized (e.g.
4:97:5483:15:14:110:493:538:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:three periods). They are thus limited for analyzing the interaction between
4:98:5558:14:15:110:237:524:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nancial and real sectors.
4:99:5584:15:14:128:495:509:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Our paper builds on our earlier work - Gertler and Kiyotaki (GK, 2015)
4:100:5654:14:15:110:492:495:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:and Gertler, Kiyotaki and Prestipino (GKP, 2016) - which analyzed bank
4:101:5724:15:14:110:494:480:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:runs in an innite horizon endowment economy. These papers characterize
4:102:5795:14:14:110:492:466:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:runs as self-fullling rollover crises, following the Calvo (1988) and Cole and
4:103:5874:14:15:110:495:452:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Kehoe (2001) models of sovereign debt crises. Both GK and GKPempha-
4:104:5941:15:14:110:496:437:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:size the complementary nature of balance sheet conditions and bank runs.
4:105:6013:14:15:110:493:423:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Balance sheet conditions a¤ect not only borrower access to credit but also
4:106:6087:15:14:110:495:408:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:whether the banking system is vulnerable to a run. In this waythe model
4:107:6158:14:15:110:495:394:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:is able to capture the highly nonlinear nature of a collapse:When bank bal-
4:108:6233:15:14:110:493:379:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ance sheets are strong, negative shocks do not push the nancial system to
4:109:6307:14:15:110:493:365:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the verge of collapse. When they are weak, the same size shockleads the
4:110:6378:15:14:110:494:350:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:economy into a crisis zone in which a bank run equilibrium exists.2While
4:111:6450:14:15:110:493:336:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:our earlier work restricted attention to a simple endowmenteconomy, here
4:112:6522:15:14:110:493:321:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:we extend the analysis to a conventional macroeconomic model. By doing
4:113:6592:14:14:110:494:307:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:so, we can explicitly capture both qualitatively and quantitatively the e¤ect
4:114:6669:14:15:110:495:293:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:of the nancial collapse on investment, output and employment. In particu-
4:115:6743:15:14:110:495:278:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:lar, we proceed to show that a calibrated version of our modelis capable of
4:116:6818:14:15:110:495:264:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:capturing the dynamics of key nancial and real variables over the course of
4:117:6894:15:14:110:190:249:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the recent crisis.
4:118:6912:14:15:128:493:235:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Also related is important recent work on occasionally binding borrowing
4:119:6983:15:14:110:493:220:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:constraints as a source of nonlinearity in nancial crises such as Mendoza
4:120:7057:14:19:110:495:206:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:(2010) and He and Krishnamurthy (2017). There, in good timesthe bor-
4:121:7125:19:15:124:494:187:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:2Some recent examples where self-fullling nancial crises can emerge depending on the
4:122:7211:15:12:110:496:172:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:state of the economy include Benhabib and Wang (2013), Bocola and Lorenzoni (2017),
4:123:7294:12:12:110:495:160:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Farhi and Maggiori (2017) and Perri and Quadrini (forthcoming). For further attempts
4:124:7378:12:12:110:493:148:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:to incorporate bank runs in macro models, see Angeloni and Faia (2013), Cooper and
4:125:7460:12:12:110:499:136:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Ross (1998), Martin, Skeie and Von Thadden (2014), Robatto (2014) and Uhlig (2010) for
4:126:7546:12:0:110:146:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:example.
5:127:7555:0:15:110:494:654:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:rowing constraint is not binding and the economy behaves much the way it
5:128:7627:15:14:110:493:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:does with frictionless nancial markets. However, a negative disturbance can
5:129:7703:14:15:110:493:625:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:move the economy into a region where the constraint is binding, amplifying
5:130:7777:15:14:110:495:610:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the e¤ect of the shock on the downturn. In a similar spirit, Brunnermeier
5:131:7850:14:14:110:495:596:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:and Sannikov (2014) generate nonlinear dynamics based on the precaution-
5:132:7922:14:15:110:496:582:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ary saving behavior by intermediaries worried about survival in the face of
5:133:7997:15:14:110:495:567:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:a sequence of negative aggregate shocks. Our approach also allows for occa-
5:134:8072:14:15:110:492:553:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:sionally binding nancial constraints and precautionary saving. However, in
5:135:8147:15:14:110:472:538:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:quantitative terms, bank runs provide the major source of nonlinearity.
5:136:8218:14:15:128:494:524:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Section 2 presents the behavior of bankers and workers, the sectors where
5:137:8291:15:14:110:495:509:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the novel features of the model are introduced. Section 3 describes the fea-
5:138:8367:14:15:110:495:495:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:tures that are standard in the New Keynesian model: the behavior of rms,
5:139:8440:15:14:110:495:480:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:price setting, investment and monetary policy. Section 4 describes the cal-
5:140:8515:14:14:110:494:466:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ibration and presents a variety of numerical exercises designed to illustrate
5:141:8592:14:15:110:493:452:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the main features of the model, including how the model can capture the
5:142:8663:15:40:110:452:437:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:dynamics of some of the main features of the recent nancial crisis.
5:143:8731:40:26:110:475:397:17:g_d0_f5:17:g_d0_f5:2  Model: outline, households, and bankers
5:144:8773:26:15:110:495:371:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:The baseline framework is a standard New Keynesian model with capital ac-
5:145:8846:15:14:110:495:356:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:cumulation. In contrast to the conventional model, each household consists
5:146:8920:14:14:110:495:342:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:of bankers and workers. Bankers specialize in making loans and thus inter-
5:147:8994:14:15:110:493:328:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:mediate funds between households and productive capital. Households may
5:148:9065:15:14:110:493:313:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:also make these loans directly, but they are less e¢cient in doing so than
5:149:9139:14:15:110:493:299:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:bankers.3On the other hand, bankers may be constrained in their ability to
5:150:9213:15:14:110:495:284:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:raise external funds and also may be subject to runs. The net e¤ect is that
5:151:9288:14:15:110:494:270:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the cost of capital will depend on the endogenously determined ow of funds
5:152:9363:15:14:110:321:255:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:between intermediated and direct nance.
5:153:9403:14:15:128:493:241:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:We distinguish between capital at the beginning of periodt,Kt, and
5:154:9469:15:14:110:495:226:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:capital at the end of the period,St:Capital at the beginning of the period is
5:155:9546:14:15:110:495:212:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:used in conjunction with labor to produce output att. Capital at the end of
5:156:9621:15:14:110:495:197:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:period is the sum of newly produced capital and the amount of capital left
5:157:9695:14:18:110:197:183:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f9:after production:
5:158:9712:18:15:124:494:165:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:3As section 2.2. makes clear, technically it is the workers within the household that are
5:159:9801:15:12:110:497:150:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:left to manage any direct nance. But since these workers collectively decide consumption,
5:160:9891:12:12:110:494:138:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:labor and portfolio choice on of behalf the household, we simply refer to them as the
5:161:9976:12:0:110:222:126:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:household going forward.

21:791:40518:14:15:110:496:328:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:a fundamental shock that induces an insolvent banking system is negligible.
21:792:40593:15:14:110:494:313:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:However, the probability of a shock that induces a bank run equilibrium is
21:793:40667:14:39:110:179:299:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:not negligible.

27:1092:51028:35:22:110:229:381:14:g_d0_f5:14:g_d0_f5:4.2  Experiments

27:1094:51119:14:15:110:491:345:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:how our model economy behaves and compares with the data. We rst show
27:1095:51189:15:14:110:494:330:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the response of the economy to a capital quality shock with and without runs
27:1096:51265:14:14:110:493:316:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:to illustrate how the model generates a nancial panic. We then compare
27:1097:51336:14:15:110:495:302:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:how runs versus occasionally binding constraints can generate nonlinear dy-
27:1098:51411:15:14:110:492:287:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:namics. Finally, we turn to an experiment that shows how the model can
27:1099:51481:14:32:110:379:273:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:replicate salient features of the recent nancial crisis.
27:1100:51538:32:22:110:463:241:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:4.2.1  Response to a capital quality shock: no bank run case
27:1101:51598:22:14:110:494:219:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:We suppose the economy is initially in a risk-adjusted steady state. Figure
27:1102:51673:14:18:110:493:205:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:1 shows the response of the economy to a negative one standarddeviation
27:1103:51744:18:16:120:499:187:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:21In practice we assume that-t+1is a truncated normal with support(-10--;10--).
27:1104:51823:16:12:110:496:171:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Given our calibration for--and--the probability that-tgoes below zero is computa-
27:1105:51904:12:0:110:164:159:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:tionally zero.
28:1106:51920:0:15:110:495:654:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:(.75%) shock to the quality of capital.22The solid line is our baseline model
28:1107:51997:15:14:110:493:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:and the dotted line is the case where there are no nancial frictions. For both
28:1108:52076:14:15:110:495:625:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:cases the shock reduces the expected return to capital, reducing investment
28:1109:52151:15:14:110:493:610:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:and in turn aggregate demand. In addition, for the baseline economy with
28:1110:52223:14:14:110:495:596:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nancial frictions, the weakening of bank balance sheets amplies the contrac-
28:1111:52301:14:15:110:495:582:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:tion in demand through the nancial accelerator or credit cycle mechanism of
28:1112:52377:15:14:110:495:567:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Bernanke Gertler and Gilchrist (1999) and Kiyotaki and Moore(1997). Poor
28:1113:52449:14:15:110:494:553:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:asset returns following the shock cause bank net worth to decrease by about
28:1114:52524:15:14:110:495:538:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f6:15%. As bank net worth declines, incentive constraints tightenand banks
28:1115:52595:14:15:110:494:524:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:decrease their demand for assets causing the price of capital to drop. The
28:1116:52669:15:14:110:495:509:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:drop in asset prices feeds back into lower bank net worth, an e¤ect that is
28:1117:52744:14:15:110:492:495:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:magnied by the extent of bank leverage. As nancial constraints tighten
28:1118:52816:15:14:110:494:480:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:and asset prices decline, excess returns rise by75basis points which allows
28:1119:52891:14:14:110:494:466:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:banks to increase their leverage by about10%:Overall, a0:75percent decline
28:1120:52965:14:15:110:493:452:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:in the quality of capital results in a drop in investment by5percent and a
28:1121:53039:15:14:110:494:437:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:drop in output by slightly more than1percent. The drop in investment is
28:1122:53110:14:15:110:493:423:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:roughly double the amount in the case absent nancial frictions, while the
28:1123:53184:15:14:110:345:408:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:drop in output is about thirty percent greater.
28:1124:53231:14:15:128:494:394:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:In the experiment of Figure 1, the economy is always ex post ina "safe
28:1125:53301:15:14:110:495:379:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:zone", where a bank run equilibrium does not exist.  Under ourparame-
28:1126:53370:14:15:110:492:365:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:trization, a bank run cannot happen in the risk-adjusted steady state: bank
28:1127:53445:15:14:110:494:350:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:leverage is too low. The dashed line in the rst panel of Figure 1 shows the
28:1128:53521:14:15:110:493:336:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:size of the shock in the subsequent period needed to push the economy into
28:1129:53595:15:14:110:493:321:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the run region:In our example, a two standard deviation shock is needed to
28:1130:53669:14:14:110:496:307:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:open up the possibility of runs starting from the risk adjusted steady state,
28:1131:53746:14:15:110:415:293:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:which is double the size of the shock considered in Figure 1.
28:1132:53807:15:14:128:495:278:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Even though in this case the economy is always in a safe regionex post,
28:1133:53878:14:15:110:494:264:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:it is possible ex ante that a run equilibrium could occur in the subsequent
28:1134:53953:15:14:110:494:249:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:period. In particular, the increase in leverage following the shock raises the
28:1135:54031:14:15:110:493:235:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:probability that a su¢ciently bad shock in the subsequent period pushes the
28:1136:54106:15:14:110:494:220:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:economy into the run region. As the top middle panel of Figure1 shows, the
28:1137:54180:14:18:110:402:206:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:overall probability of a run increases following the shock.
28:1138:54239:18:15:120:496:188:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:22In all of the experiments we trace the response of the economy to the shocks consid-
28:1139:54325:15:12:110:496:173:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:ered assuming that after these shocks capital quality is exactly equal to its conditional
28:1140:54414:12:0:110:282:161:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f16:expectations, i.e. setting future"tto0:
29:1141:54455:0:22:110:207:654:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:4.2.2  Bank runs
29:1142:54471:22:15:110:494:632:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:In the previous experiment the economy was well within a safezone. A one
29:1143:54543:15:14:110:494:617:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:standard deviation shock did not and could not produce a nancial panic. We
29:1144:54618:14:15:110:493:603:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:now consider a case where the economy starts in the safe zone but is gradually
29:1145:54696:15:14:110:494:588:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:pushed to the edge of the crisis zone, where a run equilibriumexists. We
29:1146:54768:14:15:110:494:574:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:then show how an arrival of sunspot induces a panic with damaging e¤ects
29:1147:54840:15:14:110:212:559:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:on the real economy.
29:1148:54860:14:15:128:493:545:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:To implement this experiment, we assume that the economy is hit by a
29:1149:54928:15:14:110:494:530:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:sequence of three equally sized negative shocks that push the economy to the
29:1150:55004:14:24:110:393:516:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:run threshold. That is, we nd a shock--that satises:
29:1151:55058:24:0:241:298:492:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f14:-R3= 1 +--
29:1152:55068:0:9:301:306:501:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:-
29:1153:55069:9:0:307:362:492:12:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f8:1 +--+-2-
29:1154:55078:0:35:363:368:501:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:-
29:1155:55079:35:14:110:495:466:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:where-R3is the threshold level for the capital quality below which a run is
29:1156:55154:14:15:110:499:452:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f9:possible in period3;given that the economy is in steady state in period0
29:1157:55226:15:14:110:499:437:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f7:and is hit by two equally sized shocks in periods 1 and 2, i.e.-1=-2=--:
29:1158:55298:14:15:110:494:423:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:The rst two shocks push the economy to the edge of the crisis zone. The
29:1159:55370:15:14:110:222:408:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:third pushes it just in.
29:1160:55394:14:15:128:489:394:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:The solid line in Figure 2 shows the response of the economy starting from
29:1161:55468:15:14:110:493:379:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:period two onwards under the assumption that the economy experiences a
29:1162:55538:14:15:110:494:365:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:run with arrival of a sunspot in period 3. For comparison, thedashed line
29:1163:55611:15:14:110:494:350:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:shows the response of the economy to the same exact capital quality shocks
29:1164:55685:14:15:110:444:336:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:but assuming that no sunspot is observed and so no run happens.
29:1165:55748:15:14:128:495:321:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:As shown in panel 1 the size of the threshold innovation of capital qual-
29:1166:55821:14:14:110:496:307:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ity shock turns out to be roughly equal to one standard deviation, i.e.
29:1167:55892:14:15:110:494:293:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f6:--=-:83%:, which is the size of the shock in Figure 1.  After the rst
29:1168:55962:15:14:110:495:278:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:two innovations, the capital quality is1:4%below average and the run prob-
29:1169:56036:14:15:110:493:264:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ability is about2%quarterly. The last innovation pushes the economy into
29:1170:56108:15:14:110:495:249:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the run region. When the sunspot is observed and the run occurs, bank net
29:1171:56181:14:15:110:495:235:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:worth is wiped out which forces banks to liquidate assets. Inturn, house-
29:1172:56254:15:14:110:493:220:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:holds absorb the entire capital stock. Households however are only willing to
29:1173:56331:14:15:110:494:206:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:increase their portfolio holdings of capital at a discount,which leads excess
29:1174:56408:15:14:110:495:191:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:returns to spike and investment to collapse. When the run occurs, investment
29:1175:56484:14:14:110:492:177:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:drops an additional25%resulting in an overall drop of35%. Comparing with
29:1176:56556:14:15:110:493:163:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the case of no run claries that almost none of this additional drop is due
29:1177:56631:15:14:110:494:148:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:to the capital quality shock itself: The additional drop in investment absent
29:1178:56708:14:15:110:493:134:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:a run is only 2.5%. The collapse in investment demand causes ination to
29:1179:56780:15:0:110:493:119:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:decrease and induces monetary policy to ease by reducing thepolicy rate to
30:1180:56856:0:15:110:493:654:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:slightly below zero. However, reducing the nominal interest rate to roughly
30:1181:56931:15:14:110:413:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:zero is not su¢cient to insulate output which drops by7%.
30:1182:56988:14:15:128:493:625:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:As new bankers enter the economy, bank net worth is slowly rebuilt and
30:1183:57058:15:14:110:493:610:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the economy returns to the steady state. This recovery is slowed down by a
30:1184:57132:14:14:110:494:596:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:persistent increase in the run probability following the banking panic. The
30:1185:57207:14:15:110:493:582:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:increase in the run probability reduces the amount of leverage that banks are
30:1186:57284:15:14:110:200:567:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:willing to take on.
30:1187:57303:14:15:128:493:553:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:To get a sense of the role that nominal rigidities are playing, Figure 3
30:1188:57375:15:14:110:494:538:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:describes the e¤ect of bank runs in the economy with exible prices. For
30:1189:57447:14:15:110:494:524:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:comparison, with the analogous experiment in our baseline (in Figure 2) we
30:1190:57521:15:14:110:493:509:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:hit the ex price economy with the same sequence of shocks that would take
30:1191:57595:14:15:110:494:495:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the baseline economy to the run threshold.23There are two main takeaways
30:1192:57667:15:14:110:494:480:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:from Figure 3. First, the output drop in the exible price case is only about
30:1193:57744:14:14:110:494:466:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:half that in our benchmark sticky price case. The New Keynesian features
30:1194:57816:14:15:110:493:452:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:thus magnify the e¤ects of the banking crisis. The reason is that the banking
30:1195:57893:15:14:110:493:437:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:crisis generates a steep decline in the natural rate of interest by inducing a
30:1196:57971:14:15:110:496:423:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:collapse in investment demand. As a result, in the exible price case the real
30:1197:58049:15:14:110:493:408:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:interest rate, which is equals the natural rate, drops roughly eight hundred
30:1198:58125:14:15:110:492:394:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:basis points below zero leading to a temporary expansion in consumption
30:1199:58196:15:14:110:495:379:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:demand and hence dampening the output contraction. Clearly, such a dra-
30:1200:58267:14:15:110:493:365:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:matic drop in real rates would not be feasible with nominal rigidities and a
30:1201:58343:15:14:110:496:350:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:zero lower bound. Second, even in the exible price case, a bank run will
30:1202:58416:14:15:110:495:336:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:amplify the contraction in output by inducing a large drop ininvestment
30:1203:58487:15:14:110:494:321:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:demand. In our example, relative to the no run case, the run increases the
30:1204:58561:14:31:110:452:307:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:drop in output from about one percent to three and a half percent.
30:1205:58627:31:22:110:472:276:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:4.2.3  Nonlinearities: occasionally binding constraints vs runs
30:1206:58690:22:15:110:493:254:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:We now turn to nonlinearities within our baseline model. We will start by
30:1207:58763:15:14:110:495:239:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:considering the e¤ects of occasionally binding constraints. Figure 4 shows
30:1208:58837:14:15:110:493:225:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the behavior of the economy when it transits from slack to binding nancing
30:1209:58912:15:14:110:494:210:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:(incentive) constraints. In our calibration, the risk adjusted steady state lies
30:1210:58992:14:15:110:493:196:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:at the borderline for the nancing constraint to be binding.If the shock
30:1211:59064:15:17:110:495:181:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:to capital quality is positive the constraint is slack, while it becomes bind-
30:1212:59142:17:16:120:495:164:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:23However, since in the ex price economy there is much less amplication, the ex-
30:1213:59224:16:12:110:495:148:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:post run that we consider is actually not an equilbrium. As the rst panel inthe gure
30:1214:59310:12:12:110:495:136:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:shows, even after the rst two shocks the shock that is needed to pushthe economy to the
30:1215:59398:12:0:110:412:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:threshold is still very large in the ex price economy, i.e. around -4%.
31:1216:59472:0:15:110:496:654:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ing with negative capital quality shocks. Overall, nonlinearities are present,
31:1217:59550:15:14:110:495:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:though they do not turn out to be as large as in the case of bank runs. A neg-
31:1218:59628:14:15:110:494:625:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ative capital quality shock a¤ects investment, asset prices and credit spreads
31:1219:59706:15:14:110:495:610:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:only a little more, in absolute value, than does a similar magnitude increase.
31:1220:59784:14:14:110:493:596:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:The asymmetries arising in our framework are somewhat dampened for two
31:1221:59854:14:15:110:492:582:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:reasons: First, in many frameworks the maximum leverage multiple is xed
31:1222:59926:15:14:110:493:567:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:(e.g. Mendoza, 2010). However, in our model, as the economy moves into
31:1223:59996:14:15:110:493:553:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the constrained region the maximum leverage multiple increases (see section
31:1224:60071:15:14:110:495:538:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:2.2.2). This relaxing of the leverage constraint mitigatesthe decline in real
31:1225:60148:14:15:110:495:524:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:activity and asset prices and the rise in credit spreads. Second, it is often as-
31:1226:60229:15:14:110:493:509:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:sumed that the real interest rate is xed. In our model, however, the real rate
31:1227:60308:14:15:110:492:495:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:declines as the economy weakens, which also works to dampen the decline in
31:1228:60382:15:14:110:224:480:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the constrained region.
31:1229:60405:14:14:128:493:466:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Next we consider bank runs. Figure 5 shows the response of theeconomy
31:1230:60474:14:15:110:492:452:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:to a capital quality shock starting from the same initial state considered in
31:1231:60551:15:14:110:494:437:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Figure 2. The dashed line depicts the response in the case in which no sunspot
31:1232:60629:14:15:110:492:423:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:occurs (so that a bank run cannot happen) and the solid one shows the case in
31:1233:60706:15:14:110:496:408:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:which a sunspot appears (so that a run will occur if a run equilibrium exists).
31:1234:60785:14:15:110:494:394:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:As long as capital quality shocks are above the run thresholdthe responses
31:1235:60859:15:14:110:493:379:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:are identical in the both cases since in this region a run is not possible. When
31:1236:60939:14:15:110:492:365:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the shock lies below the run threshold, however, a run equilibrium exists. In
31:1237:61016:15:14:110:494:350:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:this region, when agents observe a sunspot they run on nancial institutions
31:1238:61092:14:15:110:494:336:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:pushing the economy to an equilibrium in which banks are forced to liquidate
31:1239:61168:15:14:110:493:321:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:assets at re sale prices. The discrete and highly nonlinearbehavior during
31:1240:61243:14:14:110:495:307:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nancial crisis (which we described in Introduction) then emerges: excess
31:1241:61316:14:32:110:386:293:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:returns spike and investment and asset prices collapse.
31:1242:61371:32:22:110:363:261:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:4.2.4  Crisis experiment: model versus data
31:1243:61414:22:14:110:494:239:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:Figure 6 illustrates how the model can replicate some salient features of the
31:1244:61491:14:15:110:492:225:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:recent nancial crisis. We hit the economy with a series of capital quality
31:1245:61566:15:14:110:495:210:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:shocks over the period 2007Q4 until 2008Q3. The starting point is the begin-
31:1246:61642:14:15:110:494:196:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ning of the recession, which roughly coincides with the timecredit markets
31:1247:61716:15:14:110:496:181:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:rst came under stress following Bear Stearns losses on itsMBS portfolios.
31:1248:61791:14:14:110:494:167:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:We pick the size of the capital quality shocks to match the observed decline
31:1249:61867:14:15:110:495:153:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:in investment during this period, in panel 1. We then assume that a run hap-
31:1250:61943:15:14:110:494:138:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:pens in 2008Q4, the quarter in which Lehman failed and the shadow banking
31:1251:62016:14:0:110:493:124:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:system collapsed. The solid line shows the observed response of some key
32:1252:62090:0:15:110:495:654:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:macroeconomic variables.24The dashed line shows the response of the econ-
32:1253:62163:15:14:110:493:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:omy when a run occurs in 2008Q4 and the dotted line shows the response
32:1254:62233:14:15:110:366:625:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:under the assumption that a run does not happen.
32:1255:62281:15:14:128:493:610:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:As indicated in panel 2, the sequence of negative surprises in the quality
32:1256:62355:14:14:110:493:596:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:of capital needed to match the observed contraction in investment leads to a
32:1257:62431:14:15:110:494:582:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:gradual decline in banks net worth that matches closely the observed decline
32:1258:62507:15:14:110:495:567:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:in nancial sector equity as measured by the XLF index, whichis an index of
32:1259:62582:14:15:110:493:553:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:S&P 500 nancial stocks. Given that banks net worth is already depleted by
32:1260:62656:15:14:110:492:538:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:poor asset returns, a very modest innovation in 2008Q4 pushes the economy
32:1261:62729:14:15:110:493:524:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:into the run region. When the run occurs, the model economy generates a
32:1262:62800:15:14:110:493:509:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:sudden spike in excess returns and a drop in investment, output, consumption
32:1263:62876:14:15:110:494:495:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:and employment of similar magnitudes as those observed during the crisis
32:1264:62948:15:14:110:494:480:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:in panels 3 - 6. The dotted line shows how, absent a run, the same shocks
32:1265:63021:14:14:110:337:466:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:would generate a much less severe downturn.
32:1266:63064:14:15:128:493:452:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:The model economy also predicts a rather slow recovery following the
32:1267:63132:15:14:110:494:437:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:nancial crisis, although faster than what we observed in the data.  It is
32:1268:63206:14:15:110:489:423:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:important however to note that in the experiment we are abstracting from
32:1269:63278:15:14:110:495:408:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:any disturbances after 2008Q4. This implies a rather swift recovery of nan-
32:1270:63354:14:15:110:496:394:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:cial equity and excess returns to their long run value. On theother hand,
32:1271:63427:15:14:110:492:379:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the observed recovery of net worth and credit spreads was much slower with
32:1272:63501:14:15:110:495:365:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:both variables still far from their pre-crisis values as of today. Various factors
32:1273:63583:15:14:110:494:350:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:that are not captured in our model economy, such as a drastic change in the
32:1274:63658:14:15:110:495:336:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:regulatory framework of nancial institutions, increaseduncertainty follow-
32:1275:63733:15:14:110:493:321:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:ing the crisis and slow adjustment of household balance sheets, have likely
32:1276:63808:14:14:110:495:307:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:contributed to the very slow recovery of these nancial variables. Incorpo-
32:1277:63883:14:15:110:493:293:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:rating these factors could help the model account for the very slow recovery
32:1278:63959:15:14:110:494:278:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:of investment and employment. However we leave this extension for future
32:1279:64031:14:40:110:151:264:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:research.
32:1280:64040:40:27:110:221:224:17:g_d0_f5:17:g_d0_f5:5  Conclusion
32:1281:64053:27:14:110:494:197:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:We have developed a macroeconomic model with a banking sector where
32:1282:64120:14:14:110:495:183:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:costly nancial panics can arise.  A panic or run in our model is a self-
32:1283:64193:14:18:110:495:169:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:fullling failure of creditors to roll over their short-term credits to banks.
32:1284:64271:18:16:120:493:151:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:24For output, investment and consumption we show deviation from a trend computed
32:1285:64351:16:12:110:495:135:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:by using CBO estimates of potential output and similarly for hours worked we let the
32:1286:64435:12:0:110:338:123:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:CBO estimate of potentail labor represent the trend.
33:1287:64489:0:15:110:495:654:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:When the economy is close to the steady state a self-fullling rollover crises
33:1288:64567:15:14:110:494:639:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:cannot happen because banks have su¢ciently strong balancesheets. In this
33:1289:64640:14:15:110:496:625:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:situation, "normal size" business cycle shocks do not lead to nancial crises.
33:1290:64718:15:14:110:494:610:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:However, in a recession, banks may have su¢ciently weak balance sheet so as
33:1291:64793:14:14:110:494:596:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:to open up the possibility of a run. Depending on the circumstances either
33:1292:64867:14:15:110:493:582:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:a small shock or no further shock can generate a run that has devastating
33:1293:64940:15:14:110:494:567:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:consequences for the real economy. We show that our model generates the
33:1294:65011:14:15:110:495:553:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:highly nonlinear contraction in economic activity associated with nancial
33:1295:65085:15:14:110:494:538:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:crises. It also captures how crises may occur even in the absence of large
33:1296:65159:14:15:110:494:524:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:exogenous shocks to the economy.  We then illustrate that themodel is
33:1297:65228:15:14:110:361:509:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:broadly consistent with the recent nancial crisis.
33:1298:65279:14:15:128:496:495:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:One issue we save for further work is the role of macroprudential policy.
33:1299:65352:15:14:110:495:480:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:As with other models of macroprudential policy, externalities are present that
33:1300:65430:14:14:110:494:466:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:lead banks to take more risk than is socially e¢cient. Much ofthe literature
33:1301:65506:14:15:110:494:452:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:is based on the pecuniary externality analyzed by Lorenzoni(2008), where
33:1302:65578:15:14:110:493:437:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:individual banks do not properly internalize the exposure of the system to
33:1303:65652:14:15:110:490:423:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:asset price uctuations that generate ine¢cient volatility, but not runs. A
33:1304:65727:15:14:110:493:408:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:distinctive feature of our model is that the key externalityworks through the
33:1305:65804:14:15:110:493:394:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:e¤ect of leverage on the bank run probability: Because the run probability
33:1306:65878:15:14:110:494:379:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:depends on the leverage of the banking system as a whole, individual banks
33:1307:65952:14:15:110:492:365:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:do not fully take into account the impact of their own leverage decisions on
33:1308:66028:15:14:110:495:350:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the exposure of the entire system. In this environment, the key concern of
33:1309:66102:14:15:110:496:336:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:the macroprudential policy becomes reducing the possibility of a nancial
33:1310:66175:15:14:110:494:321:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:collapse in the most e¢cient way. Our model will permit us to explore the
33:1311:66248:14:0:110:404:307:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f6:optimal design of policies qualitatively and quantitatively.
